having multiple instances.\n   105→ * <p>\n   106→ * Here is a simple example of using the producer to send records with strings containing sequential numbers as the key/value\n   107→ * pairs.\n   108→ * <pre>\n   109→ * {@code\n   110→ * Properties props = new Properties();\n   111→ * props.put(\"bootstrap.servers\", \"localhost:9092\");\n   112→ * props.put(\"linger.ms\", 1);\n   113→ * 115→ *\n   116→ * Producer<String, String> producer = new KafkaProducer<>(props);\n   117→ * for (int i = 0; i < 100; i++)\n   118→ *     producer.send(new ProducerRecord<String, String>(\"my-topic\", Integer.toString(i), Integer.toString(i)));\n   119→ *\n   120→ * producer.close();\n   121→ * }</pre>\n   122→ * <p>\n   123→ * The producer consists of a pool of buffer space that holds records that haven't yet been transmitted to the server\n   124→ * as well as a background I/O thread that is responsible for turning these records into requests and transmitting them\n   125→ * to the cluster. Failure to close the producer after use will leak these resources.\n   126→ * <p>\n   127→ * The {@link #send(ProducerRecord) send()} method is asynchronous. When called, it adds the record to a buffer of pending record sends\n   128→ * and immediately returns. This allows the producer to batch together individual records for efficiency.\n   129→ * <p>\n   130→ * The <code>acks</code> config controls the criteria under which requests are considered complete. The default setting \"all\"\n   131→ * will result in blocking on the full commit of the record, the slowest but most durable setting.\n   132→ * <p>\n   133→ * If the request fails, the producer can automatically retry. The <code>retries</code> setting defaults to <code>Integer.MAX_VALUE</code>, and\n   134→ * it's recommended to use <code>delivery.timeout.ms</code> to control retry behavior, instead of <code>retries</code>.\n   135→ * <p>\n   136→ * The producer maintains buffers of unsent records for each partition. These buffers are of a size specified by\n   137→ * the <code>batch.size</code> config. Making this larger can result in more batching, but requires more memory (since we will\n   138→ * generally have one of these buffers for each active partition).\n   139→ * <p>\n   140→ * By default a buffer is available to send immediately even if there is additional unused space in the buffer. However if you\n   141→ * want to reduce the number of requests you can set <code>linger.ms</code> to something greater than 0. This will\n   142→ * instruct the producer to wait up to that number of milliseconds before sending a request in hope that more records will\n   143→ * arrive to fill up the same batch. This is analogous to Nagle's algorithm in TCP. For example, in the code snippet above,\n   144→ * likely all 100 records would be sent in a single request since we set our linger time to 1 millisecond. However this setting\n   145→ * would add 1 millisecond of latency to our request waiting for more records to arrive if we didn't fill up the buffer. Note that\n   146→ * records that arrive close together in time will generally batch together even with <code>linger.ms=0</code>. So, under heavy load,\n   147→ * batching will occur regardless of the linger configuration; however setting this to something larger than 0 can lead to fewer, more\n   148→ * efficient requests when not under maximal load at the cost of a small amount of latency.\n   149→ * <p>\n   150→ * The <code>buffer.memory</code> controls the total amount of memory available to the producer for buffering. records are returned to the consumer's\n            // poll call or if the offset is being reset.\n            // It can also happen under the Consumer rebalance protocol, when the consumer changes FetchResponse bytes deserialized into MemoryRecords\n  - Each RecordBatch decompressed (if compressed)\n  - Each Record extracted:\n    - Key bytes → keyDeserializer → K object\n    - Value bytes → valueDeserializer → V object\n  - ConsumerRecord<K, V> created with all metadata:\n    - topic, partition, offset, timestamp, key, value, headers, leaderEpoch\n\n### **T10: Consumer Application Delivery**\n- **Location**: `ClassicKafkaConsumer.poll()` → `onConsume()` interceptors\n- **File**: `/workspace/clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/ClassicKafkaConsumer.java`\n- **What changes**: ConsumerRecords → InterceptedConsumerRecords → application objects\n- **Process**:\n  -
